Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Qisas Across Gender, Age, and Health Conditions
Rulings on qisas between different categories of persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that qisas is obligatory between persons of different gender, age, and health conditions, and explain the principle of equality in ismah.

Core Idea
Equality in ismah (inviolability) is the sole criterion for qisas, regardless of gender, age, or physical condition.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq establishes the foundational principle that qisas applies between persons of different physical attributes as long as they are equal in inviolability of blood. The text systematically lists cases where qisas is obligatory, and explains why this broad application is necessary to prevent fitnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pairs listed in the text
List the categories: man/woman, adult/child, healthy/blind, healthy/chronically ill (zamin), healthy/person with missing limbs, healthy/insane.
These are all examples of different physical states.
2
Extract the general principle
The text states that qisas runs between them because of equality in ismah. Ismah is the inviolability of life, which all Muslims share equally.
This is the key legal criterion.
3
Note the consensus and the anomalous report
The killing of a man for a woman is by consensus, except for a report from Ali that is rejected because qisas and diyah cannot combine for one act.
Understand why the report is unsound.
4
Understand the rationale for broad application
If other attributes (like physical strength) were considered, the door of qisas would close, leading to fitnah.
This shows the overarching legal policy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرجل بالمرأة والكبير بالصغير، والصحيح بالأعمى، وبالزمن، وبناقص الأطراف، وبالمجنون، والولد بالوالد ولا يقتل الرجل بالولد، هو من طال مرضه زمانا. والرجل بالمرأة إلخ إلى قوله : "وبالمجنون" يعني يقتل الرجل الصحيح بهؤلاء، وهو معطوف على ما تقدم من قوله: "والحر بالحر لا على ما يليه من قوله ولا يقتلان بمستأمن" وإنما جرى القصاص بينهم؛ لوجود المساواة بينهم في العصمة والمساواة فيها هي المعتبرة في هذا الباب ولو اعتبرت فيما ورائها لانسد باب القصاص ولظهر الفتن. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٦٩/٩] بالمرأة إلخ: وقتل الرجل بالمرأة قصاصا بالإجماع إلا ما روي عن علي الله أنه قال في الرجل إذا قتل امرأة: "إن أوليائها بالخيار إن شاءوا أخذوا ديتها، وإن شاءوا أعطوا القاتل نصف ديته وقتلوه"، وهذا لا يصح؛ الفعل الواحد لا يتعلق به قصاص وغرم في النفس الواحدة كما لا يجب بالفعل الواحد مهر واحد، ولأن التكافؤ معتبر في محل القصاص، ومحل القصاص الروح، فإذا تساويا في حقن الدم وجب القصاص وإن اختلفا في غير ذلك، ولهذا لم يجب القصاص بين الأطراف المختلفة؛ لأن التساوي في محل القصاص لم يوجد. (فتح الله المعين) والولد بالوالد : أي يقتل الولد بالوالد لما تلونا وروينا من العمومات ولما ذكرنا من المعاني. ولا يقتل الرجل إلخ: لقوله علية "لا يقاد الوالد بولده، ولا السيد بعبده"، ولأن الوالد لا يقتل ولده غالبا لوفور شفقته فيكون ذلك شبهة في سقوط القصاص، ولأن الأب لا يستحق العقوبة بولده؛ لأنه سبب لإحيائه، فمن المحال أن يكون الولد سببا لإفنائه ولهذا لا يقتله إذا وجده في صف المشركين مقاتلا أو زانيا وهو محصن. وطولب بالفرق بين هذا وبين من زنى بابنته وهو محصن؛ فإنه يرجم، أجيب بأن الرجم حق الله على الخصوص بخلاف القصاص، لا يقال: فيجب أن يحد إذا زنى بجارية ابنه؛ لأنا نقول: ثبت له حق الملك بقوله علي: "أنت ومالك لأبيك". (فتح)
And the man for the woman, and the adult for the child, and the healthy for the blind, and the chronically ill, and the one with missing limbs, and the insane, and the child for the parent, but the man is not killed for the child. 'al-zamin' is he whose illness lasted long. 'Al-rajul bi al-mar'ah' etc. means the healthy man is killed for these. It is conjoined to what precedes: 'the free for the free', not to what follows. Qisas runs between them because of equality in ismah, and equality in ismah is the consideration in this chapter. Were other things considered, the door of qisas would be closed and fitnah would appear. ... The killing of a man for a woman is by consensus except what is narrated from Ali that he said: 'The heirs of the woman have the choice: if they wish, they take her diyah; if they wish, they give the killer half his diyah and kill him.' But this is not sound; a single act cannot entail both qisas and monetary compensation for one life, just as a single act cannot entail two mahr. And because equivalence is considered in the locus of qisas, and the locus of qisas is the soul. So when they are equal in inviolability of blood, qisas becomes obligatory, even if they differ in other respects. Hence, qisas is not obligatory between different body parts, because equivalence in the locus of qisas is not found. (Fath Allah al-Mu'in) 'Al-walad bil-walid': meaning the child is killed for the parent, due to the general texts we recited and the meanings we mentioned. 'But the man is not killed for the child': due to his saying: 'A parent is not executed for his child, nor a master for his slave.' And because a parent generally does not kill his child due to abundant compassion, so that constitutes a doubt (shubha) that drops qisas. And because the father does not deserve punishment through his child; he is the cause of the child's life, so it is impossible that the child becomes the cause of his destruction. Hence, he is not killed if he finds the child fighting in the ranks of the polytheists or committing adultery while married. And it was demanded to distinguish between this and the case of one who commits adultery with his daughter while married; he is stoned. The answer: stoning is a right of Allah exclusively, unlike qisas. It cannot be said that he should be flogged if he commits adultery with his son's slave-girl; because we say: the right of ownership is established for him by his saying: 'You and your property belong to your father.' (Fath)
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage provides a series of rulings on qisas between persons of different gender, age, and health, and also the asymmetry between parent and child. The general principle: qisas applies whenever there is equality in ismah (inviolability), even if physical attributes differ. Thus, a man is killed for a woman, an adult for a child, a healthy person for a blind or chronically ill person, etc. This is by consensus, with an anomalous report from Ali which is rejected because qisas and diyah cannot apply simultaneously for the same act. Regarding parent-child: a child is killed for killing his parent (based on general texts), but a parent is not killed for killing his own child. The proof is the hadith: 'A parent is not executed for his child, nor a master for his slave.' Additionally, the parent's natural compassion creates a shubha, and it would be contradictory for a child to be the cause of his parent's death when the parent is the cause of his life. The passage also addresses objections: why does the parent get stoned for adultery with his daughter but not executed for killing his son? Because stoning is a pure right of Allah, while qisas involves a personal right and shubha prevents it. Similarly, a father is not flogged for zina with his son's slave-girl because the father has a right of ownership.

Key Terms
زمن (zamin): A person with a chronic, long-term illness.
عصمة (isma): Inviolability, protection of life and honor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the general principle that makes qisas obligatory between a healthy man and a blind man?
A) Equality in physical strength
B) Equality in ismah (inviolability)
C) Consent of the heirs
D) The killer's wealth

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, qisas is obligatory between any two persons who are equal in ismah, regardless of gender, age, or health.

Parent-Child Qisas Asymmetry
Ruling on parent-child qisas asymmetry with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a child is killed for killing a parent but a parent is not killed for killing a child, and identify the proofs and the shubha argument.

Core Idea
A parent is not executed for killing his child due to hadith and shubha of compassion; the child is executed for killing the parent.

This passage addresses the asymmetry in qisas between parent and child. The child is subject to qisas for killing the parent based on general texts, but the parent is exempt due to a specific hadith and the concept of shubha derived from natural parental compassion. The text also distinguishes this ruling from other cases like zina with one's daughter.

Guided Path
1
State the two rulings
Child is killed for parent; parent is not killed for child.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the proof for killing the child
General texts (Quran and hadith) commanding qisas for murder apply to child killing parent.
No specific exemption for the child as killer.
3
Identify the proof for exempting the parent
Hadith: 'A parent is not executed for his child, nor a master for his slave.' Also the shubha of natural compassion.
The hadith is explicit.
4
Analyze the shubha argument
A parent's abundant compassion makes it unlikely they would intentionally kill their child, creating a legal doubt that drops qisas.
This is a unique Hanafi reasoning.
5
Distinguish from other cases
Why is a parent stoned for zina with his daughter? Because stoning is a pure right of Allah, not affected by shubha. Why is a father not flogged for zina with his son's slave-girl? Because of the father's right of ownership.
These distinctions clarify the scope of the shubha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرجل بالمرأة والكبير بالصغير، والصحيح بالأعمى، وبالزمن، وبناقص الأطراف، وبالمجنون، والولد بالوالد ولا يقتل الرجل بالولد، هو من طال مرضه زمانا. والرجل بالمرأة إلخ إلى قوله : "وبالمجنون" يعني يقتل الرجل الصحيح بهؤلاء، وهو معطوف على ما تقدم من قوله: "والحر بالحر لا على ما يليه من قوله ولا يقتلان بمستأمن" وإنما جرى القصاص بينهم؛ لوجود المساواة بينهم في العصمة والمساواة فيها هي المعتبرة في هذا الباب ولو اعتبرت فيما ورائها لانسد باب القصاص ولظهر الفتن. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٦٩/٩] بالمرأة إلخ: وقتل الرجل بالمرأة قصاصا بالإجماع إلا ما روي عن علي الله أنه قال في الرجل إذا قتل امرأة: "إن أوليائها بالخيار إن شاءوا أخذوا ديتها، وإن شاءوا أعطوا القاتل نصف ديته وقتلوه"، وهذا لا يصح؛ الفعل الواحد لا يتعلق به قصاص وغرم في النفس الواحدة كما لا يجب بالفعل الواحد مهر واحد، ولأن التكافؤ معتبر في محل القصاص، ومحل القصاص الروح، فإذا تساويا في حقن الدم وجب القصاص وإن اختلفا في غير ذلك، ولهذا لم يجب القصاص بين الأطراف المختلفة؛ لأن التساوي في محل القصاص لم يوجد. (فتح الله المعين) والولد بالوالد : أي يقتل الولد بالوالد لما تلونا وروينا من العمومات ولما ذكرنا من المعاني. ولا يقتل الرجل إلخ: لقوله علية "لا يقاد الوالد بولده، ولا السيد بعبده"، ولأن الوالد لا يقتل ولده غالبا لوفور شفقته فيكون ذلك شبهة في سقوط القصاص، ولأن الأب لا يستحق العقوبة بولده؛ لأنه سبب لإحيائه، فمن المحال أن يكون الولد سببا لإفنائه ولهذا لا يقتله إذا وجده في صف المشركين مقاتلا أو زانيا وهو محصن. وطولب بالفرق بين هذا وبين من زنى بابنته وهو محصن؛ فإنه يرجم، أجيب بأن الرجم حق الله على الخصوص بخلاف القصاص، لا يقال: فيجب أن يحد إذا زنى بجارية ابنه؛ لأنا نقول: ثبت له حق الملك بقوله علي: "أنت ومالك لأبيك". (فتح)
And the man for the woman, and the adult for the child, and the healthy for the blind, and the chronically ill, and the one with missing limbs, and the insane, and the child for the parent, but the man is not killed for the child. 'al-zamin' is he whose illness lasted long. 'Al-rajul bi al-mar'ah' etc. means the healthy man is killed for these. It is conjoined to what precedes: 'the free for the free', not to what follows. Qisas runs between them because of equality in ismah, and equality in ismah is the consideration in this chapter. Were other things considered, the door of qisas would be closed and fitnah would appear. ... The killing of a man for a woman is by consensus except what is narrated from Ali that he said: 'The heirs of the woman have the choice: if they wish, they take her diyah; if they wish, they give the killer half his diyah and kill him.' But this is not sound; a single act cannot entail both qisas and monetary compensation for one life, just as a single act cannot entail two mahr. And because equivalence is considered in the locus of qisas, and the locus of qisas is the soul. So when they are equal in inviolability of blood, qisas becomes obligatory, even if they differ in other respects. Hence, qisas is not obligatory between different body parts, because equivalence in the locus of qisas is not found. (Fath Allah al-Mu'in) 'Al-walad bil-walid': meaning the child is killed for the parent, due to the general texts we recited and the meanings we mentioned. 'But the man is not killed for the child': due to his saying: 'A parent is not executed for his child, nor a master for his slave.' And because a parent generally does not kill his child due to abundant compassion, so that constitutes a doubt (shubha) that drops qisas. And because the father does not deserve punishment through his child; he is the cause of the child's life, so it is impossible that the child becomes the cause of his destruction. Hence, he is not killed if he finds the child fighting in the ranks of the polytheists or committing adultery while married. And it was demanded to distinguish between this and the case of one who commits adultery with his daughter while married; he is stoned. The answer: stoning is a right of Allah exclusively, unlike qisas. It cannot be said that he should be flogged if he commits adultery with his son's slave-girl; because we say: the right of ownership is established for him by his saying: 'You and your property belong to your father.' (Fath)
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage provides a series of rulings on qisas between persons of different gender, age, and health, and also the asymmetry between parent and child. The general principle: qisas applies whenever there is equality in ismah (inviolability), even if physical attributes differ. Thus, a man is killed for a woman, an adult for a child, a healthy person for a blind or chronically ill person, etc. This is by consensus, with an anomalous report from Ali which is rejected because qisas and diyah cannot apply simultaneously for the same act. Regarding parent-child: a child is killed for killing his parent (based on general texts), but a parent is not killed for killing his own child. The proof is the hadith: 'A parent is not executed for his child, nor a master for his slave.' Additionally, the parent's natural compassion creates a shubha, and it would be contradictory for a child to be the cause of his parent's death when the parent is the cause of his life. The passage also addresses objections: why does the parent get stoned for adultery with his daughter but not executed for killing his son? Because stoning is a pure right of Allah, while qisas involves a personal right and shubha prevents it. Similarly, a father is not flogged for zina with his son's slave-girl because the father has a right of ownership.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): A legal doubt that prevents qisas, here the natural compassion of a parent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Quranic verse 'a life for a life' does not apply.
B) The hadith 'A parent is not executed for his child.'
C) The child's property belongs to the parent.
D) The parent can pay diyah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a child is executed for killing a parent, but a parent is never executed for killing a child, due to the hadith and the shubha of natural compassion.

Muslim Killed for a Dhimmi: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Qisas
Ruling with proof and refutation of Shafi'i objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on killing a Muslim for a dhimmi in qisas, explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i objection, and apply the distinction between harbi and dhimmi to the interpretation of the relevant hadith.

Core Idea
A Muslim is killed for a dhimmi because immunity is based on abode, not religion.

Can a Muslim be executed for killing a non-Muslim? The Hanafi school says yes, if the victim is a dhimmi. This is a classic inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'is, who cite a hadith that seems to prohibit it. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi proof, the Shafi'i objection, and the Hanafi response that resolves the apparent conflict by distinguishing between a harbi and a dhimmi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its scope
The passage states the Hanafi position: a Muslim is killed (yuqtal) for a dhimmi. Note that this applies only to intentional killing of a dhimmi, not a harbi (enemy combatant) or musta'man (temporary resident).
The dhimmi is a protected non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state.
2
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i cites the hadith 'A believer is not killed for an unbeliever' and argues that there is no equality between the two at the time of the crime; also, unbelief (kufr) is a permissible cause (mubih) of bloodshed, creating doubt that prevents qisas.
The Shafi'i objection rests on the unconditional reading of the hadith and the idea that the victim's kufr makes his blood less protected.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between a harbi (whose blood is permissible due to active enmity) and a dhimmi (whose blood is protected by covenant). Equality in immunity (isma) is established by residence in dar al-Islam and being subject to taklif, not religion. The hadith about a believer not being killed for an unbeliever refers specifically to a harbi, as indicated by the context.
The Hanafi argue that the same hadith that seems to forbid qisas for a non-Muslim actually proves it for a dhimmi when properly contextualised.
4
Confirm the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical consequence: Hanafis allow a Muslim to be executed for killing a dhimmi; Shafi'is do not. This affects the law of qisas in a multi-faith society.
The dispute is not merely theoretical; it has real implications for criminal justice.
5
Recognise the authority of the Hanafi position
The passage concludes 'kadha fi al-Hidayah', indicating that the Hanafi position is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school.
Al-Hidayah is a foundational Hanafi fiqh text by al-Marghinani.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يوجب القصاص وما لا يوجد
والمسلم بالذمي، ولا يقتلان بالمستأمن، والرجل بالمرأة والكبير بالصغير، والصحيح
المسلم والذمي

والمسلم بالذمي: أي يقتل المسلم بالذمي خلافا للشافعي رحلته له قوله عليه: "لا يقتل مؤمن بكافر"، ولأنه لا مساواة بينهما وقت الجناية، وكذا الكفر ،مبيح، فيورث الشبهة، ولنا ما روي أن النبي عليه قتل مسلما بذمي، ولأن المساواة في العصمة ثابتة نظرا إلى التكليف أو الدار والمبيح كفر المحارب دون المسالم، وقتل الذمي بالذمي يؤذن بانتفاء الشبهة، والمراد بما روي الحربي لسياقه، ولا ذو عهد في عهده"؛ لأن المعطوف يكون مغائرا للمعطوف عليه كذا في "الهداية".
What necessitates qisas and what does not: And the Muslim for the dhimmi, and neither of them is killed for the musta'man, and the man for the woman and the adult for the child, and the healthy [person] ... the Muslim and the dhimmi? meaning he is killed ... for the blind, and for the chronically ill, and for the amputee, and for the insane, and the child for the parent, and the man is not killed for the child. He (commentator) said: "He whose illness lasted a long time" meaning that the child is not killed for the parent. And the Muslim for the dhimmi: i.e. the Muslim is killed for the dhimmi, contrary to al-Shafi'i, may God have mercy on him, due to his (the Prophet's) statement: "A believer is not killed for an unbeliever," and because there is no equality between them at the time of the crime, and also unbelief is a permissible thing (mubih), so it creates doubt. Our proof is what was narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) killed a Muslim for a dhimmi, and because equality in immunity (isma) is established considering taklif (religious obligation) or the abode (dar), and the permissible thing (mubih) is the unbelief of the combatant (harbi), not the peaceful one. And the killing of a dhimmi for a dhimmi indicates the removal of doubt, and what is meant by what was narrated is the harbi due to its context, and 'no one of covenant is in his covenant' because the conjunct is different from the conjoined, as in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with a full inter-madhhab dispute. The author states the Hanafi position: a Muslim is executed in qisas for intentionally killing a dhimmi. He then presents the Shafi'i objection: the Prophet said 'A believer is not killed for an unbeliever' and there is no equality between the two at the time of the crime; furthermore, unbelief is a 'mubih' (permissible cause of bloodshed) which creates doubt (shubha) preventing qisas. The Hanafi response: the cited hadith refers to a harbi (enemy combatant), not a dhimmi under Muslim protection. Equality in immunity (isma) is established by residence in the abode of Islam or by being subject to religious obligations, not by religion. The permissibility of blood (mubih) applies only to the harbi, whose blood is not protected. The fact that a dhimmi is executed for killing another dhimmi shows that there is no doubt regarding their immunity. The passage concludes by referencing al-Hidayah for the resolution of the textual issue.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment for intentional homicide or wounding, where the perpetrator suffers the equivalent harm.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state who lives under protection of the covenant of dhimma, paying jizya.
عصمة (isma): Legal immunity of life and property that prevents permissible killing.
مبيح (mubih): A factor that makes bloodshed legally permissible, such as kufr in the case of a harbi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The Prophet expressly ordered it in all cases.
D) The dhimmi's life is more valuable than a Muslim's.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a Muslim is killed in qisas for intentionally killing a dhimmi because immunity (isma) is determined by abode and legal capacity, not religion, and the relevant hadith is specified to apply only to enemy combatants.

Inheriting Qisas Against One's Father Drops
Explains the drop of inherited qisas against a father.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a child inherits qisas against his parent and explain the underlying principle that causes the qisas to drop.

Core Idea
A child who inherits qisas against his own father cannot execute it; the qisas drops.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a subtle intersection of qisas and inheritance. The ruling seems counterintuitive: why would an inherited right disappear? The answer lies in a fundamental Hanafi principle that prohibits a child from being the agent of punishment against his parent. Let's explore the scenario and the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Recall the Hanafi legal maxim: a child cannot execute qisas against his father. This is based on the idea that a parent is not liable to retaliation by a child.
This principle is derived from the general prohibition of a child causing harm to a parent.
2
Examine the Scenario
Consider a father who kills his wife's brother. The wife (victim's sister) is the sole heir and inherits the right to qisas. Before she executes it, she dies, and her son (from that same father) inherits the qisas right.
The son inherits the qisas right from his mother.
3
Apply the Principle
The son now has a qisas claim against his own father. Applying the principle, the son cannot execute it. Therefore, the qisas right drops entirely.
It does not transfer to anyone else; it is nullified.
4
Consider an Analogous Case
The same ruling applies if the father kills his wife (the son's mother). The son cannot execute qisas against his father, so the qisas drops.
The relationship of paternity is the barring factor.
5
Confirm the Consistency
This ruling is consistent across Hanafi sources (e.g., al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Ramz al-Haqa'iq). There is no intra-madhab disagreement.
The ruling is relied upon (mufta bihi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن ورث قصاصا على أبيه ،سقط. وإن ورث قصاصا إلخ لما ذكرنا أن الابن لا يستوجب العقوبة على أبيه، وصورة المسألة فيما إذا قتل الأب أخ امرأته ولا وارث له غيرها ثم ماتت امرأته قبل أن يقتص منه، فإن ابنها منه يرث القصاص الذي لها على أبيه، فسقط لما ذكرنا تكملة البحر الرائق: ۷۰/۹] وكذا لو قتل امرأته ليس لابنها منه أن يقتله، فيسقط القصاص. رمز الحقائق: ٤٢٥/٢]
And if he inherits qisas against his father, it drops. (Commentary:) 'And if he inherits qisas etc.' because we have mentioned that the son does not deserve punishment on his father. The scenario is: when the father kills his wife's brother, and she has no heir other than him, then his wife dies before he [the father] is retaliated against. Then her son from him [the father] inherits the qisas that she had against her father [i.e., his father], so it drops for the reason we mentioned. Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 9/70. Similarly, if he kills his wife, her son from him does not have the right to kill him, so the qisas drops. Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/425.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage gives a specific scenario. The principle is that a child cannot be the executor of qisas against his father. The example: a father kills his wife's brother. The wife (the victim's sister) is the only heir and thus has the right to qisas. But before she executes it, she dies. Her son from that same father inherits the qisas right. Now the son has a qisas claim against his own father. Since the son cannot execute qisas against his father, the qisas drops. Similarly, if the father kills his wife, the son (from that marriage) cannot kill his father. The ruling is consistent: the filial relationship prevents qisas.

Key Terms
ورث (waritha): To inherit the right to qisas.
يسقط (yasqutu): The qisas right is nullified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The qisas drops.
C) The son must forgive.
D) The state executes qisas.

Key Takeaway
When a child inherits the right to qisas against his own parent, the qisas drops and cannot be executed.

Qisas for Killing a Mukatab: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Details the rulings when a mukatab is killed intentionally, with disagreement among the three imams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three scenarios of killing a mukatab and state the qisas ruling according to each of the three Hanafi imams, identifying the basis of their disagreement.

Core Idea
When a mukatab is killed, qisas depends on the continuity of the master's right; change in basis creates ikhtilaf.

This lesson examines the rulings on intentional killing of a mukatab (a slave under a manumission contract). The passage presents three scenarios and the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. By analyzing the basis of the master's right at the time of injury and death, we see why the imams differ in one scenario and agree in others. This sharpens our understanding of how legal cause (sabab) affects qisas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage discusses three cases: (1) mukatab killed, leaves insufficient wealth, only master as heir; (2) mukatab killed, leaves insufficient wealth, has a non-master heir also; (3) mukatab killed, leaves sufficient wealth and a non-master heir. Note that the phrase 'or he does not leave sufficient wealth...' in the text actually refers to the second scenario.
The third scenario is mentioned at the end: if the mukatab leaves enough wealth and an heir other than the master, all agree no qisas.
2
Analyze the first scenario (ikhtilaf)
In scenario 1 (insufficient wealth, only master as heir), Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold qisas is obligatory because the master's right is consistent: at injury, right due to ownership; at death, right due to wala' (inheritance). Muhammad argues no qisas because the basis differs (ownership vs. inheritance), creating ambiguity (shubha).
This is the core ikhtilaf. The difference stems from whether the change in legal cause affects the right to qisas.
3
Analyze the second scenario (consensus)
In scenario 2 (insufficient wealth, non-master heir also), all three imams agree qisas is executed. Reason: the master's right remains consistent—at injury he has ownership, and at death the kitaba is voided by the mukatab's inability, so the mukatab dies a slave and the master inherits as owner. Hence no ambiguity.
The presence of a non-master heir does not create ambiguity here because the master's right is continuous.
4
Analyze the third scenario (consensus against qisas)
When the mukatab leaves sufficient wealth and an heir other than the master, all agree no qisas. This is because the mukatab's ability to pay the kitaba means he might be considered free at death (according to 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud), making the heir the guardian of qisas; but if considered a slave (according to Zayd ibn Thabit), the master would be the guardian. This uncertainty (shubha) prevents qisas.
The ikhtilaf between sahaba on the status of the dying mukatab creates the ambiguity.
5
Compare with mu'taq al-ba'd
The passage contrasts the mukatab with a partially free slave (mu'taq al-ba'd). For the latter, if killed and leaves insufficient wealth, no qisas by consensus because his partial freedom is not rescinded, so the right to qisas does not vest in the master at death.
This comparison highlights the specificity of the mukatab's suspended ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مكاتب قتل عمدا القصاص. مكاتب قتل عمدا إلخ: هاتان مسألتان حكمهما عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف أنه يقتص المكاتب، وعند محمد حكم الثانية كما قالا، وحكم الأولى: أنه لا يقتص، فالمسألة الأولى: أن مكاتبا قتله رجل عمدا وترك المكاتب مالا يفي ببدل الكتابة، والحال أن وارثه سیده فقط، فعندهما يقتص من القاتل؛ لأنه لا اشتباه في ولي القصاص، فإنه هو المولى في الحالين؛ لأن حق القصاص له وقت الجراحة لبقاء الرق ووقت الموت أيضا بحكم الولاء، وعند محمد لا قصاص فيها؛ لأن السبب مختلف، فإن وقت الجناية كان له حق القصاص لأجل الملك، ووقت الموت يجب له بحكم الميراث، فصار اختلاف : وترك وفاء، ووارثه سيده فقط، أو لم يترك وفاء وله وارث يقتص، وإن ترك وفاء المكاتب و وارثا لا،. أو لم يترك وفاء إلخ: هذه هي المسألة الثانية، وحكمها عندهم جميعا أن يقتص من القاتل؛ لأن الجراحة وقعت، والولاية للمولى، وحصل الموت وهو المستحق؛ لأن الكتابة بطلت بموته عاجزا، وعاد إلى الرق، وإذا ثبت الاستحقاق له في الحالين حال الجراحة والموت كان له القصاص كما في العبد القن، بخلاف معتق البعض إذا قتل ولم يترك وفاء، حيث لا يجب القصاص؛ لأن العتق في البعض لا ينفسخ بموته عاجزا. (فتح ، عيني) وارث حر أو ليس له وارث فالتقييد بقوله: "وله" "وارث اتفاقي. و إن ترك وفاء إلخ: أي إن ترك المكاتب الذي قتل عمدا وفاء ووارثا غير المولى لا يقتص بالإجماع لاشتباه من له الحق؛ لأنه إن مات حرا كما قال علي وابن مسعود ما فالقصاص للوارث وإن مات عبدا كما قال زيد بن ثابت منه فالقصاص للمولى. [ رمز الحقائق: ٤٢٥/٢]
A mukatab killed intentionally: qisas. (Commentary:) 'A mukatab killed intentionally etc.': There are two cases. Their ruling according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is that the mukatab is subject to qisas [i.e., the killer is executed]. According to Muhammad, the ruling of the second case is as they said, but the ruling of the first case: there is no qisas. The first case: a man kills a mukatab intentionally, and the mukatab leaves wealth insufficient to cover the kitaba, and his only heir is his master. In this case, according to them, qisas is executed from the killer because there is no ambiguity about the guardian of qisas; he is the master in both [the time of injury and death] because the right to qisas belongs to the master at the time of injury due to remaining slavery, and at the time of death also by virtue of wala. According to Muhammad, there is no qisas in this case because the basis [of the right] differs: at the time of the crime, the master had the right due to ownership, but at the time of death, the right is due to inheritance, so there is a difference. ... And [the mukatab] leaves sufficient wealth, and his only heir is his master; or he does not leave sufficient wealth and has an heir [who is not the master], then qisas is executed. And if the mukatab leaves sufficient wealth and an heir [other than the master], then no qisas. (Commentary:) 'Or he does not leave sufficient wealth etc.': This is the second case. Its ruling according to all of them is that qisas is executed from the killer because the injury occurred, the guardianship [for qisas] belongs to the master, and death occurred while he [the master] is the entitled party, because the kitaba is canceled by his death in a state of inability [to pay], and he returns to slavery. When the entitlement is proven for him in both states (injury and death), he has the right to qisas, just as in the case of a full slave. Unlike the partially free slave (mu'taq al-ba'd) if he is killed and leaves insufficient wealth, where qisas is not obligatory because the manumission of a part is not rescinded by his death in a state of inability. (Fath, 'Ayni) 'Heir free or has no heir': the restriction 'with an heir' is agreed upon. 'And if he leaves full payment etc.': i.e., if the mukatab who was killed intentionally leaves full payment [to cover the kitaba] and an heir other than the master, then no qisas by consensus because of ambiguity regarding who has the right. Because if he died free (as said by 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud), then qisas is for the heir; but if he died a slave (as said by Zayd ibn Thabit), then qisas is for the master. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/425)
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The passage discusses two scenarios when a mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission) is killed. First scenario: the mukatab dies from the injury, leaving insufficient wealth to pay the kitaba, and his only heir is his master. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say qisas is executed because the master's right is clear (ownership at injury, wala at death). Muhammad says no qisas because the basis of the right differs (ownership vs. inheritance), creating ambiguity. Second scenario: the mukatab leaves insufficient wealth but has an heir other than the master (e.g., a free child). All three agree that qisas is executed because the master's right is consistent. If the mukatab leaves enough wealth and an heir other than the master, all agree no qisas because of uncertainty over the mukatab's status (free or slave).

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has a kitaba contract to earn his freedom.
ولاء (wala'): Patronage/clientage that transfers to the master upon the slave's death if he is free.
معتق البعض (mu'taq al-ba'd): A slave partially manumitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second scenario (mukatab leaves insufficient wealth but has a non-master heir), what is the ruling according to all three Hanafi imams?
A) Qisas is executed because the master's right is continuous.
B) No qisas because the non-master heir creates ambiguity.
C) Diya is paid by the killer.
D) The master must free another slave.

Key Takeaway
Qisas for killing a mukatab hinges on whether the master's right is based on a consistent cause; any change in the legal basis can create a shubha that bars qisas.

Qisas for Killing a Mortgaged Slave Requires Consent of Both Parties
Ruling on qisas for a mortgaged slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a mortgaged slave is killed and explain why both parties must consent, and determine the outcome if they disagree.

Core Idea
Qisas for a mortgaged slave cannot be executed without the mortgagee's consent due to his collateral right.

This lesson explores a specific ruling in the intersection of qisas (retaliation) and rahn (mortgage). When a mortgaged slave is killed, the killer cannot be executed until both the owner (rahin) and the creditor (murtahin) agree. This ensures the creditor's security interest is not extinguished without compensation. Understanding this ruling clarifies how competing rights are balanced in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their rights
First, identify the mortgagor (rahin) who owns the slave but pawned it, and the mortgagee (murtahin) who holds it as collateral for a debt.
The slave is owned by the rahin but the murtahin has a claim over it as security.
2
Analyze the conflict of rights
Why can't the owner alone execute qisas? Executing qisas kills the killer, but then the slave's value is lost, harming the creditor.
The creditor has no ownership but a right to hold the slave as collateral.
3
Derive the condition for qisas
Both parties must consent. The owner's right to qisas is conditional on the creditor agreeing to forfeit the collateral.
If the creditor does not consent, the killer pays the slave's market value, which becomes new collateral.
4
Determine the alternative ruling
If they disagree, qisas is not performed; instead, the killer must pay the slave's value (qima), and that value becomes a new collateral in place of the slave.
This protects the creditor's right while allowing the owner to receive compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قتل عبد الرهن لا يقتص حتى يجتمع الراهن والمرتهن. يعني إن قتل أحد عبد الرهن لا يقتص القاتل حتى يجتمع الراهن والمرتهن فإذا اجتمعا كان للراهن أن يستوفي القصاص؛ لأن المرتمن لا ملك له، فلا يلي القصاص، والراهن لو تولى استيفاء القصاص بطل حق المرتمن؛ لأنه لو قتل القاتل بطل حق المرتمن في الدين لهلاك الرهن بلا بدل فشرط اجتماعهما ليسقط حق المرتمن برضاه، وإن اختلفا فلهما القيمة تكون رهنا مكانه. (فتح، عيني)
And if a mortgaged slave is killed, qisas is not executed until the mortgagor and mortgagee come together. Means if someone kills a mortgaged slave, the killer is not executed until the mortgagor and mortgagee come together. When they come together, the mortgagor has the right to execute qisas because the mortgagee has no ownership, so he does not have guardianship of qisas. If the mortgagor alone executes qisas, the right of the mortgagee would be nullified because if he kills the killer, the mortgagee's right in the debt would be lost due to the destruction of the collateral without compensation. So the condition of their meeting is to drop the mortgagee's right with his consent. If they disagree, then the value [of the slave] is taken and becomes collateral in its place. (Fath, 'Ayni)
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This is a ruling on qisas when the victim is a mortgaged slave (rahn). The killer cannot be executed until both the mortgagor (the owner who pawned the slave) and the mortgagee (the creditor) consent. The reason: the mortgagor has ownership and can demand qisas, but executing qisas destroys the collateral, harming the mortgagee. Therefore, the mortgagee must agree to forfeit his right in the slave. If they disagree, then the killer must pay the slave's value, which becomes collateral in place of the slave.

Key Terms
عبد الرهن (abdu al-rahn): A slave that is given as collateral for a debt.
راهن (rahin): The mortgagor, the owner who pawns the slave.
مرتهن (murtahin): The mortgagee, the creditor holding the pawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mortgaged slave is killed and the mortgagor wants qisas but the mortgagee objects, what happens?
A) Qisas is executed anyway.
B) The killer is set free.
C) The killer pays the slave's value, which becomes collateral.
D) The mortgagee must forgive.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school balances the owner's right to qisas with the creditor's security interest in a mortgaged slave, requiring mutual consent or substitution of value.

Guardianship over Qisas for the Insane Victim
Explains who has authority to execute or settle qisas for an insane person (ma'tuh).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three guardians (father, judge, wasi) and their respective powers over the qisas right of an insane victim, and explain the reasoning behind each limitation.

Core Idea
Only the father can execute qisas or forgive; the judge can execute qisas; the wasi can only settle for diya.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, as expanded in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, clarifies the authority of different guardians over the qisas right of an insane victim (ma'tuh). Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly applying the law of retaliation when the victim lacks legal capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three potential guardians
List the father, the judge, and the wasi (executor) as the guardians considered by the text.
The 'waliy' mentioned in the first line refers to the father or judge, not other relatives.
2
Determine each guardian's permissible actions
For each guardian, note whether they can execute qisas, settle for diya, or forgive. The father can do qisas and settle, but not forgive. The judge can do qisas (according to later scholars). The wasi can only settle.
Forgiveness is explicitly prohibited for the father and, by extension, anyone else.
3
Trace the legal reasoning
The text gives a rational (aqli) justification: qisas is for vengeance and pertains to the person; the father has guardianship over the person (like in marriage). Settlement is beneficial; forgiveness is pure loss without benefit.
This reasoning links the power to the type of guardianship (wilaya ala al-nafs).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the judge
Later scholars (mutakhkhirin) allow the judge to execute qisas for a minor without a guardian, but al-Natafi disagreed. The mufta bihi is the later scholars' view.
This shows the evolution of the school's position over time.
5
Apply to a scenario
If an insane man is killed and his father is alive, the father chooses qisas or diya. If the father is dead and no wasi, the judge executes qisas. If a wasi exists, he can only settle, not execute or forgive.
The wasi's limitation mirrors his limited authority in marriage (he cannot marry off the victim).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأب أي القاتل المعتوه القود والصلح لا العفو بقتل وليه، والقاضي كالأب، والوصي يصالح فقط. يعني إذا قتل رجل قريبا للمعتوه، فلولي المعتوه استيفاء القصاص وله أن يصالح. تكملة البحر: ۷۵/۹] أما القصاص؛ فلأنه للتشفي، ودرك الثأر، وكل ذلك راجع إلى النفس، ولأبيه ولاية على نفسه، فيليه كالنكاح، بخلاف الأخ وأمثاله حيث لا يكون لهم ولاية استيفاء قصاص وجب للمعتوه، وأما الصلح، فلأنه أنفع القود، وهذا إذا صالح على قدر الدية أو أكثر منه، وإن صالح على أقل منه لا يصح، وتجب الدية كاملة، وأما العفو؛ فلأنه إبطال لحقه بلا عوض ولا مصلحة فلا يجوز [رمز الحقائق: ٤٢٥/٢] والقاضي كالأب يعني أن القاضي يملك استيفاء القصاص في الصغير الذي لا ولي له، وهو قول المتأخرين من أصحابنا، وذكر الناطفي أنه لا يملك تكملة البحر الرائق: ۷٦/۹] والوصي يصالح إلخ: يعني ليس له القود ولا العفو، أما القود؛ فلأنه من باب الولاية على النفس حتى لا يملك تزويجه وأما العفو، فلأن الأب لا يملكه فالوصي أولى؛ ثم إطلاق قوله يشمل الصلح عن النفس، واستيفاء القصاص في الطرف، وذكر في كتاب الصلح أن الوصي لا يملك الصلح في النفس؛ لأن الصلح فيها بمنزلة الاستيفاء، وهو لا يملك الاستيفاء، والمذكور هنا = له من
And for the father of the insane (ma'tuh) is the right to execute qisas and to settle, but not to forgive. The judge is like the father. The wasi can only settle. Means if a man kills a relative of the insane person, then the guardian of the insane person has the right to execute qisas and to settle. Completion of al-Bahr: 9/75. As for qisas, because it is for vengeance and achieving retaliation, all of which pertains to the soul, and the father has guardianship over his person, so he carries it out like marriage. Unlike the brother and similar ones, who do not have guardianship to execute qisas for the insane person. As for settlement, it is more beneficial than qisas, and this is if he settles for the full diya or more. If he settles for less, it is not valid and the full diya is obligatory. As for forgiveness, it is invalidating his right without compensation or benefit, so it is not permissible. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/425) The judge is like the father: he has the authority to execute qisas for a minor who has no guardian. This is the view of the later scholars. Al-Natafi mentioned he does not have that authority. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 9/76) The wasi can only settle: meaning he does not have [the authority of] qisas or forgiveness. As for qisas, it is a type of guardianship over the person, like he does not have the authority to marry him. As for forgiveness, because the father does not have it, so the wasi is more [restricted]. Then the application of his statement includes settlement for the person and execution of qisas for limbs. And it is mentioned in the Book of Settlement that the wasi does not have the authority to settle for the person because settlement in that case is like execution, and he does not have authority of execution. And what is mentioned here = to him from.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage outlines the powers of guardians over the qisas right of an insane victim (ma'tuh). The father has full authority: he can execute qisas, or settle for diya (blood money), but he cannot forgive outright. The judge is like the father: he can execute qisas for a minor with no guardian, though some (al-Natafi) disagree. The wasi (executor) has the least authority: he can only settle for diya, not execute qisas or forgive. The reasoning: qisas is a matter of vengeance, which relates to the victim's person; the father has guardianship over the person (like in marriage), so he can execute. Settlement is beneficial, so it's allowed. Forgiveness would dispose of the right without benefit, so it's not allowed.

Key Terms
معتوه (ma'tuh): An insane person who lacks legal capacity.
ولي (waliy): Guardian; in this context, the father or judge.
وصي (wasiy): Executor appointed by the father to manage affairs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can the father execute qisas for an insane victim?
A) Because he is the closest relative.
B) Because he has guardianship over the person (wilayah ala al-nafs).
C) Because he has financial guardianship (wilayah ala al-mal).
D) Because the ma'tuh appointed him.

Key Takeaway
The father has broad authority over qisas for an insane victim; the judge has similar authority when no father exists; the wasi is severely limited to settlement only.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas for a Mukatib: Two Scenarios
Ruling on qisas for a mukatib with two scenarios and consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios dictating qisas for a mukatib and explain the reasoning behind each ruling.

Core Idea
Qisas for a mukatib depends on his wealth and heir: if no wealth, qisas; if wealth and a free heir, no qisas.

A mukatib (slave under kitabah) occupies a unique position: he is part slave, part free. When he commits murder, the question of qisas becomes tied to his status at death. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on when qisas is executed and when it is not, based on the mukatib's financial situation and the identity of his heir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main scenarios
Read the passage and list the two conditions: (1) mukatib does not leave wealth, (2) mukatib leaves wealth and an heir other than the master. Note the outcomes for each.
The text also mentions a sub-scenario: if he leaves no wealth but has an heir, qisas is executed.
2
Understand the legal reasoning for the first scenario
When the mukatib leaves no wealth, his kitabah is voided by death while unable to pay, and he reverts to full slavery. The master is the sole heir and has the right to claim qisas, just as for an ordinary slave (qinn).
Contrast with a part-freed slave (mu'atbaq ba'd), where freedom does not revert, so no qisas.
3
Analyze the second scenario and the consensus
When the mukatib leaves wealth and an heir other than the master, his status at death is uncertain: he could be free (if wealth suffices) or slave (if not). This uncertainty prevents qisas by consensus (ijma).
The Sahabi difference: Ali and Ibn Mas'ud said free status => qisas for heir; Zaid ibn Thabit said slave => qisas for master.
4
Derive the practical ruling
Apply the rule: qisas is executed only when the master is the undisputed heir (mukatib dies penniless). If a free heir exists and wealth is present, qisas is suspended due to ambiguity.
This is the mufta bihi position (zahir al-riwayah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وترك وفاء، ووارثه سيده فقط، أو لم يترك وفاء وله وارث يقتص، وإن ترك وفاء المكاتب و وارثا لا أو لم يترك وفاء إلخ: هذه هي المسألة الثانية، وحكمها عندهم جميعا أن يقتص من القاتل؛ لأن الجراحة وقعت، والولاية للمولى، وحصل الموت وهو المستحق؛ لأن الكتابة بطلت بموته عاجزا، وعاد إلى الرق، وإذا ثبت الاستحقاق له في الحالين حال الجراحة والموت كان له القصاص كما في العبد القن، بخلاف معتق البعض إذا قتل ولم يترك وفاء، حيث لا يجب القصاص؛ لأن العتق في البعض لا ينفسخ بموته عاجزا. (فتح ، عيني) وارث حر أو ليس له وارث فالتقييد بقوله: "وله" "وارث اتفاقي. و إن ترك وفاء إلخ: أي إن ترك المكاتب الذي قتل عمدا وفاء ووارثا غير المولى لا يقتص بالإجماع لاشتباه من له الحق؛ لأنه إن مات حرا كما قال علي وابن مسعود ما فالقصاص للوارث وإن مات عبدا كما قال زيد بن ثابت منه فالقصاص للمولى. [ رمز الحقائق: ٤٢٥/٢]
And he left wealth, and his heir is only his master, or he did not leave wealth and he has an heir, then qisas is executed. And if the mukatib leaves wealth and an heir, then no qisas. Commentary: 'Or he did not leave wealth, etc.': This is the second issue. Its ruling according to all of them is that qisas is executed from the killer because the injury occurred, the guardianship belongs to the master, and death occurred while he is the entitled one because the contract of kitabah is voided by his death while unable, and he returns to slavery. When entitlement is established for him in both states – at the time of injury and death – he has the right to qisas like an ordinary slave. Unlike a part-freed slave if he kills and does not leave wealth, where qisas is not incumbent because the freedom in part is not annulled by his death while unable. (Fath, Ayni) 'And if he leaves wealth etc.': That is, if the mukatib who killed intentionally leaves wealth and an heir other than the master, qisas is not executed by consensus due to uncertainty as to who has the right; because if he dies as a free person, as Ali and Ibn Mas'ud said, then qisas is for the heir; and if he dies as a slave, as Zaid ibn Thabit said, then qisas is for the master. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/425)
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on qisas when a mukatib (a slave under a contract of manumission) commits murder. The ruling distinguishes two scenarios: first, if the mukatib does not leave wealth and has an heir (who is his master only), qisas is executed; if he does not leave wealth but has an heir [free], qisas is also executed. Second, if the mukatib leaves wealth and an heir other than the master, qisas is not executed by consensus because it is uncertain whether he died as a free person (making qisas for the heir) or as a slave (making qisas for the master). The Hanafi position aligns with the view that if injured and died while the kitabah is voided, the master is the rightful claimant. The commentary also clarifies that this differs from the case of a part-freed slave, where qisas is not required if he dies without wealth, as his freedom does not revert.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered a contract of manumission (kitabah) and is obligated to pay for his freedom in installments.
قصاص (qiṣāṣ): Retributive justice, specifically the execution of the murderer as a punishment for taking a life unlawfully.
إجماع (ijmāʿ): Consensus of the scholars; here, consensus that qisas is not executed when the heir is uncertain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mukatib commits murder and leaves no wealth, and his heir is only his master, what is the ruling on qisas?
A) Qisas is not executed because the mukatib was a slave.
B) Qisas is executed because the master is the sole heir and the mukatib died a slave.
C) Qisas is executed only if the victim's family demands it.
D) The mukatib is freed and no qisas applies.

Key Takeaway
The execution of qisas for a mukatib hinges on whether his death leaves no wealth (qisas) or leaves wealth and a free heir (no qisas), due to uncertainty over his status.

Qisas — Retaliation

The Right to Qisas When a Mortgaged Slave Is Killed
Ruling on qisas for killing a pawned slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for killing a mortgaged slave and explain why the mortgagee's consent is required.

Core Idea
Qisas for a mortgaged slave requires the mortgagee's consent, lest his security be lost.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains a specific interaction between the laws of qisas and rahn. The mortgagee has a security interest in the slave but no ownership. If the slave is killed, the pawnor (owner) has the right to qisas, but exercising it would destroy the mortgagee's security without his approval. Therefore, the law requires the mortgagee's presence and consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the passage to determine what act is being discussed and what the initial ruling is. The act is killing a mortgaged slave. The ruling: qisas is not executed until both the pawnor and mortgagee come together.
2
Understand the rights of each party
Identify the legal interests. The pawnor (rahan) owns the slave and thus has the right to qisas. The mortgagee (murtahin) holds the slave as security for a debt; he has a right of retention but no ownership.
Ownership is key: only the owner can claim qisas.
3
Analyze the condition of mutual presence
Why must both be present? The pawnor alone executing qisas would destroy the mortgagee's security interest. The condition allows the mortgagee to consent to the loss of his security. If he does not consent, qisas cannot proceed.
The mortgagee's consent nullifies his right to the pawn.
4
Note the alternative if they disagree
If the pawnor and mortgagee disagree on whether to execute qisas, then no qisas occurs. Instead, the value of the slave is assessed and held as a new pawn to protect the mortgagee's debt.
This preserves the mortgagee's security.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و إن قتل عبد الرهن لا يقتص حتى يجتمع الراهن والمرتهن و إن قتل عبد الرهن إلخ: يعني إن قتل أحد عبد الرهن لا يقتص القاتل حتى يجتمع الراهن والمرتهن فإذا اجتمعا كان للراهن أن يستوفي القصاص؛ لأن المرتمن لا ملك له، فلا يلي القصاص، والراهن لو تولى استيفاء القصاص بطل حق المرتمن؛ لأنه لو قتل القاتل بطل حق المرتمن في الدين لهلاك الرهن بلا بدل فشرط اجتماعهما ليسقط حق المرتمن برضاه، وإن اختلفا فلهما القيمة تكون رهنا مكانه. (فتح، عيني)
And if someone kills a mortgaged slave, qisas is not executed until the mortgagor and mortgagee come together. Commentary: 'And if someone kills a mortgaged slave etc.': That is, if someone kills a mortgaged slave, the killer is not executed until the mortgagor and mortgagee both present themselves. When they do, the mortgagor may exact qisas, because the mortgagee has no ownership and thus cannot undertake qisas. If the mortgagor alone exacts qisas, it would invalidate the mortgagee's right; because if the killer is killed, the mortgagee's right to the debt would be voided due to the destruction of the pawn without compensation. Therefore, the condition of their meeting is to nullify the mortgagee's right by his consent. If they disagree, then the value [of the slave] is taken and held as a pawn in its place. (Fath, Ayni)
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where a mortgaged slave (rahn) is killed. The ruling is that qisas cannot be carried out until both the pawnor (mortgagor) and the pawnee (mortgagee) are present together. The reason is that the mortgagee has no ownership right in the slave, only a security interest, so he cannot claim qisas. If the pawnor alone exacts qisas, he would destroy the mortgagee's security without the mortgagee's consent. Thus, both must agree; if they do, the pawnor executes qisas. If they disagree, the slave's value is paid and held as a new pawn to protect the mortgagee's debt.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A pledge or pawn; a property given as security for a debt.
مرتهن (murtahin): The creditor who holds the pawn; the pawnee.
راهن (rāhin): The debtor who gives the pawn; the pawnor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Qisas for a mortgaged slave cannot be executed without the mortgagee's consent; otherwise, the value becomes a new pawn.

Qisas — Retaliation

Guardian's Authority in Qisas for Insane and Minor Victims
Ruling on guardians' authority in qisas for insane/minor victims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the different authorities of the father, judge, and executor regarding qisas and settlement for an insane or minor homicide victim, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The father may exact qisas or settle; the judge may exact qisas; the executor may only settle.

In cases where the homicide victim is insane or a minor, who holds the right to seek retribution or compensation? The Hanafi school distinguishes between guardians based on their relationship and authority over the victim's person and property. This lesson unpacks the nuanced rules from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, clarifying who may act and why.

Guided Path
1
Identify the guardians and victim status
The victim is either insane (ma'tuh) or a minor (sabi). The guardians are the father, the judge (qadi), and the executor (wasi). Determine which guardian is acting.
2
List the three possible actions per guardian
For each guardian, check whether they may exact qisas, accept a settlement (sulh) for diya, or forgive (afw) without compensation. The text specifies each combination.
Father: qisas + sulh, not afw. Judge: qisas (like father). Executor: only sulh, no qisas or afw.
3
Understand the legal reasoning
Qisas is for vengeance (soul), so only the father (who has authority over the insane person's soul) can exact it. Settlement is for wealth, so even the executor can do it. Forgiveness nullifies the right without benefit, so it is not allowed.
Text: 'qisas is for satisfaction and redress of vengeance... father has authority over his soul'
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on judge's authority
Al-Natiqi said the judge cannot exact qisas for a minor with no guardian. Later scholars (mutakhkhirin) say he can. The mufta bihi is that the judge can exact qisas.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., an executor tries to exact qisas), determine whether it is valid and cite the rule.
The executor cannot exact qisas because that is not within his authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأب أي القاتل المعتوه القود والصلح لا العفو بقتل وليه، والقاضي كالأب، والوصي يصالح فقط المعتوه جهة الحق كاختلاف المستحق، فلا يثبت القصاص، وبه قال زفر وأجيب عنه بأن اختلاف السبب لا يفضي إلى المنازعة من الفتح والعيني بتوضيح وزيادة) ولأب المعتوه إلخ: يعني إذا قتل رجل قريبا للمعتوه، فلولي المعتوه استيفاء القصاص وله أن يصالح. تكملة البحر: ٧٥/٩] أما القصاص؛ فلأنه للتشفي، ودرك الثأر، وكل ذلك راجع إلى النفس، ولأبيه ولاية على نفسه، فيليه كالنكاح، بخلاف الأخ وأمثاله حيث لا يكون لهم ولاية استيفاء قصاص وجب للمعتوه، وأما الصلح، فلأنه أنفع القود، وهذا إذا صالح على قدر الدية أو أكثر منه، وإن صالح على أقل منه لا يصح، وتجب الدية كاملة، وأما العفو؛ فلأنه إبطال لحقه بلا عوض ولا مصلحة فلا يجوز [رمز الحقائق: ٤٢٥/٢] والقاضي كالأب يعني أن القاضي يملك استيفاء القصاص في الصغير الذي لا ولي له، وهو قول المتأخرين من أصحابنا، وذكر الناطفي أنه لا يملك تكملة البحر الرائق: ٧٦/٩] والوصي يصالح إلخ: يعني ليس له القود ولا العفو، أما القود؛ فلأنه من باب الولاية على النفس حتى لا يملك تزويجه وأما العفو، فلأن الأب لا يملكه فالوصي أولى؛ ثم إطلاق قوله يشمل الصلح عن النفس، واستيفاء القصاص في الطرف، وذكر في كتاب الصلح أن الوصي لا يملك الصلح في النفس؛ لأن الصلح فيها بمنزلة الاستيفاء، وهو لا يملك الاستيفاء، والمذكور هنا = له من والصبي كالمعتوه وللكبار القود قبل كبر الصغار، وإن قتله بمر يقتص إن أصابه في الحكم المذكور أي للأولياء الكبار الحديد، وإلا لا كالخنق والتغريق، لا يقتص هو المذكور في الجامع الصغير؛ لأن المقصود من الصلح المال، والوصي يتولى التصرف فيه كما يتولى الأب، بخلاف القصاص؛ لأن المقصود منه التشفي، وهو مختص بالأب وقالوا: القياس أن لا يملك التصرف في الطرف كما بينهم. لا يملكه في النفس، وفي الاستحسان يملكه؛ لأن الأطراف يسلك بها مسلك الأموال رمز الحقائق: ٤٢٦/٢]
And for the father of the killer (or the victim?) of the insane person: qisas and settlement (sulh) are permissible, but not forgiveness (afw). And the judge is like the father, and the executor may only settle. (The insane person as a party to the right is like a dispute among the entitled, so qisas is not established. Zufar said this, and it was answered that difference in cause does not lead to conflict. From Fath and Ayni with clarification and addition.) Commentary: 'And for the father of the insane person etc.': That is, if a man kills a relative of an insane person, then the guardian of the insane person may exact qisas and may also make a settlement. (Takmilat al-Bahr: 9/75) As for qisas, it is for satisfaction and redress of vengeance, all of which pertains to the soul, and the father has authority over his [the insane person's] soul, so he undertakes it like marriage, unlike the brother and the like, who have no authority to exact qisas for the insane person. As for settlement, it is because it is more beneficial than retaliation, but only if the settlement is for the full amount of diya or more; if less, it is not valid and full diya is due. As for forgiveness, it is to nullify his right without compensation or benefit, so it is not permissible. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/425) 'And the judge is like the father' means the judge has the authority to exact qisas for a minor who has no guardian, which is the view of the later Hanafi scholars; al-Natiqi mentioned that he does not have that authority. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 9/76) 'And the executor may only settle' means he has neither the right to qisas nor forgiveness. As for qisas, it is a matter of authority over the person, and he does not have the authority to marry him; as for forgiveness, the father does not have it, so the executor is even less entitled. Then, the general wording includes settlement for a life and exacting qisas for a limb. It is mentioned in the book of Sulh that the executor cannot settle for a life because settlement in that case is equivalent to exacting, and he cannot exact. And what is mentioned here is from him. And the minor is like the insane person. And for the adult heirs, qisas may be exacted before the minors attain majority, and if he kills him with a mirr, qisas is exacted if he strikes him with the iron in the ruling mentioned, i.e., for the adult guardians, otherwise not, like strangulation and drowning, no qisas. This is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir, because the purpose of settlement is wealth, and the executor handles it like the father, unlike qisas, because its purpose is vengeance, and it is exclusive to the father. They said: by analogy, he does not have authority over the limb as he does not over the life, but by istihsan he has authority because limbs are treated like wealth. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/426)
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage details the authority of guardians in cases of homicide when the victim is an insane person (ma'tuh) or a minor (sabi). The father (or grandfather) of the insane victim has the right to either exact qisas or settle for diya (blood money), but cannot forgive without receiving compensation because that would nullify the victim's right without benefit. The qadi (judge) has similar authority for a minor without a guardian. The wasi (executor) can only settle (take diya); he cannot exact qisas or forgive. The minor (sabi) is treated like the insane person. The passage also discusses the case of adult and minor heirs: adult heirs can exact qisas before minors come of age, according to Abu Hanifa, while the Sahibayn disagree. Finally, it addresses a separate issue: killing by a digging tool (mirr) where the ruling depends on the part of the tool used (iron vs. wood) and compares it to strangulation/drowning, which do not incur qisas according to Abu Hanifa but do according to the Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i.

Key Terms
معتوه (maʿtūh): An insane person who lacks legal capacity due to mental incapacity.
وصي (waṣī): The executor of a will or guardian appointed by the father to manage the estate and care for minors.
صلح (ṣulḥ): A settlement agreement, particularly accepting diya in lieu of qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He may only accept a settlement (diya), not exact or forgive.
C) He may only exact qisas, but not settle or forgive.
D) He has no authority; only the father or judge can act.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the father and judge may exact qisas for an insane or minor victim, but the executor can only settle for diya; forgiveness without compensation is not allowed.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas When Heirs Include Both Adults and Minors
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas timing with mixed-age heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of qisas execution when heirs are both adults and minors, and apply Abu Hanifa's position that adults may execute immediately, citing the dalil from the incident of 'Ali.

Core Idea
Adult heirs may execute qisas immediately, even with minor co-heirs, because the right is indivisible and the Companions upheld this.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two students (Sahibayn) on whether adult heirs can execute qisas at once when the victim has minor children. The dispute turns on the nature of the right – indivisible or shared – and the authority of adults over minors. We will explore the proofs and the preferred opinion.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling: adult heirs may execute qisas before minors reach majority.
This is the mufta bihi view.
2
Identify the opposing view
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that execution must wait until minors become adults.
Their reasoning: qisas is a shared right and adults have no authority over minors.
3
Follow the opposing proof
Examine the Sahibayn's dalil: qisas cannot be partially executed nor fully executed without authority over minors, so delay is necessary.
They analogise to a case where one co-heir is absent.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa's evidence: the historical incident of 'Ali's qisas executed in the presence of Companions without objection, establishing tacit consensus. Also, the right is indivisible, vesting completely in each heir.
The possibility of forgiveness from minors is theoretical and severed immediately.
5
Determine the thamarah
Practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, immediate execution; under Sahibayn, delay until minors reach majority.
Also note the consensus cases: if adult is a financial guardian (father/grandfather) he may execute immediately; if a stranger, he cannot.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللكبار القود قبل كبر الصغار وللكبار القود إلخ : يعني إذا كان القصاص مشتركا بأن قتل رجل، وله أولاد كبار وصغار، فللكبار أن يقتلوا القاتل قبل أن يبلغ الصغار، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا ليس لهم ذلك حتى يبلغ الصغار؛ لأن القصاص مشترك تكملة البحر الرائق: ۷۷/۹] ولا يمكن استيفاء البعض؛ لعدم التجزي، ولا الكل؛ لعدم الولاية عليهم، وفيه إبطال حقهم فيؤخر إلى إدراكهم، كما إذا كان بين كبيرين أحدهما غائب. وللإمام ما روي أن عبد الرحمن بن ملجم حين قتل عليا له قتل به، وقد كان في أولاد عليه صغار، ولم ينتظر بلوغهم، وكان ذلك بمحضر من الصحابة من . نكير، فحل محل الإجماع؛ ولأنه حق لا يتجزأ؛ لثبوته بسبب لا يتجزأ، فيثبت لكل كملا كولاية الإنكاح ولهذا لو استوفاه بعض الأولياء، لا يضمن شيئا للقاتل، فلو لم يكن له قتله لضمن كالأجنبي، وكذا لا يضمن للباقين، واحتمال العفو من الصغير منقطع في الحال، بخلاف الكبير الغائب، ولو كان الكبير وليا للصغير ممن يملك التصرف في المال كالأب والجد يستوفيه الكبير قبل بلوغ الصغير بالإجماع، وإن كان وليا للصغير ممن لا يملك التصرف في المال كالأخ والعم، فعلى الخلاف، فإن كان الكبير أجنبيا من الصغير لا يملك الكبير الاستيفاء بالإجماع. (فتح)
And for the adult heirs, qisas may be exacted before the minors attain majority. Commentary: 'And for the adult heirs etc.': That is, if qisas is shared because a man is killed and he has adult and minor children, then the adults may kill the murderer before the minors reach puberty. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say they do not have that authority until the minors grow up, because qisas is shared. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 9/77) It is not possible to exact part of it because it is indivisible, nor to exact all of it because they have no authority over the minors, and that would nullify their rights, so it must be delayed until they mature, just as if the right is between two adults when one is absent. (Fath) The evidence for the Imam (Abu Hanifa) is what was narrated: When 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Muljam killed 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), he was killed in retaliation, even though 'Ali had minor children, and they did not wait for them to reach puberty. This was done in the presence of the Companions without any objection, so it took the place of consensus. Also, because it is a right that cannot be divided, since it is established by an indivisible cause, it is established completely for each, like the right of guardianship in marriage. For this reason, if one of the guardians exacts it, he does not owe anything to the killer, and if he did not have the right to kill, he would be liable like a stranger, and similarly he is not liable to the remaining heirs. The possibility of forgiveness from the minor is severed immediately, unlike the absent adult. If the adult is a guardian of the minor who has authority over financial matters, like the father or grandfather, then the adult may execute qisas before the minor's puberty by consensus. If the adult is a guardian of the minor who does not have authority over financial matters, like the brother or uncle, then the dispute applies. If the adult is a stranger to the minor, then the adult cannot execute qisas by consensus. (Fath)
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the execution of qisas when the victim has both adult and minor children as heirs. According to Abu Hanifa, the adult heirs may execute the qisas immediately, before the minors attain majority. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, arguing that qisas is a shared right and cannot be executed partially, nor can the adults act on behalf of the minors without authority, so execution must be delayed until the minors are mature. Abu Hanifa's evidence is the historical incident when 'Ali ibn Abi Talib was killed, and the executor was his son? Actually the account mentions 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Muljam killed 'Ali, and the qisas was carried out despite 'Ali having minor children, and the Companions did not object, implying consensus. The reasoning is that qisas is an indivisible right established by an indivisible cause so it vests fully in each heir, and the possibility of forgiveness from a minor is not present in reality. However, if the adult is a guardian with financial authority (like father or grandfather), he can execute by consensus; if not (like brother or uncle), the dispute remains. If the adult is a stranger to the minor, he cannot execute by consensus.

Key Terms
قود (qawd): Synonym for qisas; execution of the murderer.
صغار (ṣighār): Minors, particularly children who have not reached puberty.
إجماع (ijmāʿ): Consensus; here, the Companions' tacit acceptance of immediate qisas for 'Ali's killer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They must wait until the minors reach puberty.
B) They can execute qisas immediately without waiting.
C) They can only execute qisas if the minors forgive the murderer.
D) They must seek permission from the judge first.

Key Takeaway
Adult heirs may execute qisas immediately even if there are minor co-heirs, because the right is indivisible and the Companions upheld this.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Qisas for Homicide by a Digging Tool (Mirr) and Strangling/Drowning
Ruling on qisas when death is caused by a specific tool or by strangulation/drowning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for killing with a mirr and distinguish the conditions under which qisas applies versus diya.

Core Idea
For qisas, the tool matters: a cutting edge triggers retaliation; otherwise, only blood money.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq details the fiqh of qisas (retaliation) when a victim is killed using a specific digging tool (mirr) or by strangulation/drowning. The Hanafi school distinguishes between methods that involve a sharp, cutting instrument and those that do not, affecting whether qisas or diya is obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Tool
The passage deals with killing using a 'mirr' (a digging tool with an iron edge) and by strangulation or drowning. Determine which part of the tool causes death.
The mirr has three parts: the iron edge, the back of the iron, and the wooden handle.
2
Apply Consensus Rulings
If the iron edge strikes, qisas is due by consensus. If the back of the iron strikes and causes a wound, qisas is also due by consensus.
Consensus (ijma) confirms qisas in these scenarios.
3
Examine the Wounding Condition Dispute
When the back of the iron strikes without wounding, there is a difference: the apparent narration says qisas without requiring a wound; al-Tahawi's narration requires a wound.
The text prefers the apparent narration as the relied-upon view.
4
Determine Ruling for the Wooden Part
If only the wooden part strikes, no qisas is due; only diya is obligatory.
This is analogous to strangulation and drowning, which also yield only diya according to Abu Hanifa.
5
Compare Strangling/Drowning and Note Ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds that strangulation and drowning do not incur qisas, only diya. The Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i require qisas. The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's, but habitual offenders may be executed by the ruler as siyasa.
The ikhtilaf arises from differing interpretations of the Qur'anic command for qisas.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ملتقطا من الكتب بتوضيح) كالخنق والتغريق: أي لا يجب القصاص في العود، وتجب الدية، كما لا يجب القصاص في الخنق والتغريق، وتجب الدية فيهما عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما وعند الشافعي عليه القصاص غير أن عندهما يستوفي حزا، وعنده يغرق، قال في "الأصل": وإن خنق رجلا حتى مات فعلى قول أبي حنيفة الله لا قصاص ولكن إن اعتاد ذلك، فالإمام يقتله سياسة. (ملا مسكين بزيادة)
And if he kills him with a mirr, qisas is exacted if he strikes him with the iron, otherwise not, like strangulation and drowning, no qisas. This is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir. Because the purpose of settlement is wealth, and the executor handles wealth like the father, unlike qisas, because its purpose is vengeance, and it is exclusive to the father. They said: by analogy he does not have authority over the limb as he does not over the life, but by istihsan he has authority because limbs are treated like wealth. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/426) 'And if he kills him with a mirr etc.': The word 'mirr' is with a fatha on the meem and shadda on the ra', and it is a long stick with a wide piece of iron at its head, above which is a wide piece of wood on which a man places his foot, and he digs the earth with it. That is, if he kills him with a mirr, if the edge hits him, the killer is subjected to qisas, otherwise not. The matter has several aspects: either he strikes him with the iron edge, the back of the iron, or the wood. If he strikes him with the iron edge, qisas by consensus. If he strikes him with the back of the iron, then if it wounds, qisas also by consensus; if it does not wound, there are two narrations from the Imam: in the apparent narration, qisas is exacted because wounding is not a condition; according to al-Tahawi's narration, wounding is a condition, so no qisas. This dispute about the condition of wounding was mentioned at the beginning of the book, so recall it. If the iron does not hit him but the wood hits him, no qisas, rather diya is obligatory so that blood is not wasted. (Compiled from books with clarification) 'Like strangulation and drowning': That is, qisas is not obligatory for the wood, and diya is obligatory, just as qisas is not obligatory for strangulation and drowning, and diya is obligatory for both according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and al-Shafi'i, qisas is required, except that according to the two he is executed by swords, and according to al-Shafi'i by drowning. He said in al-Asl: And if he strangles a man until he dies, according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, there is no qisas, but if it is habitual, the Imam may execute him for policy (siyasa). (Mulla Miskeen with addition)
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage covers the details of qisas when a person is killed using a specific tool called a 'mirr' (a digging implement), and compares it to death by strangulation or drowning. For the mirr, the ruling varies depending on which part of the tool causes the death: if the iron edge strikes, qisas is due by consensus; if the back of the iron causes a wound, qisas also by consensus; if the back of the iron does not wound, there is a difference of narration within the Hanafi school (the apparent view is qisas without requiring a wound, while al-Tahawi's narration requires a wound). If only the wooden part strikes, no qisas but only diya (blood money) is due. As for strangulation and drowning, Abu Hanifa holds that no qisas is required (only diya), because these are not considered 'direct' killing by a sharp instrument. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and al-Shafi'i hold that qisas is required, with the method of execution being similar to the killing method (drowning for drowning, etc.). The text also mentions that if someone habitually uses such methods, the ruler may execute him as a discretionary punishment (siyasa).

Key Terms
مرّ (mirr): A digging tool with an iron edge at the end of a long handle, used for digging; when used as a weapon, the ruling depends on which part strikes.
خنق (khanaq): Strangling; causing death by compressing the neck.
تغريق (taghrīq): Drowning; causing death by immersing in water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Obligatory only if the killer intended to kill.

Key Takeaway
For qisas, the instrument must be sharp and cutting; otherwise, only diya is due, and for strangulation/drowning, Abu Hanifa's view of no qisas is the relied-upon position.
